3.7.3.5 Engineer Reconnaissance – Tunnel Report
The tunnel report is supplemental to the road report or a rail network evaluation.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.
2) Start Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
3) End Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
4) Tunnel Name. Clear text box entry up to 50 characters if the tunnel has a known name.
5) Tunnel Direction. Expressed as a two-digit code. First digit is S: Single direction or B:
Bidirectional and second digit equates to actual cardinal direction for single direction: E:
East, W: West, N: North, S: South and 1: East/West or 2: North/South for bidirectional
tunnels.
6) Tunnel Number. If the tunnel has a corresponding number expressed as a seven-digit
alpha-numeric value with special characters (XXXXXX).

55

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
7) Tunnel Media Through Type. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the
clear text option; A: Subaqueous, B: Rock, C: Soil
8) Tunnel Through Feature. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the
clear text option; M: Mountain, W: Water
9) Tunnel Length. Expressed as a five-digit numeric position value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
10) Tunnel Type. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text
option; 1: Road, 2: Rail, 3: Waterway, 4: Pedestrian
11) Rail Tunnel Tracks. Number of tracks expressed as two-digit numeric value as whole
numbers (XX).
12) Roadway Tunnel Lanes. Number of lanes expressed as a two-digit numeric value as
whole numbers (XX).
13) Roadway Tunnel Width. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
14) Tunnel Vertical Clearance. Expressed as a five-digit numeric and single digit alpha value
in feet as whole numbers (XXXXX).
15) Tunnel Horizonal Clearance. Expressed as a five-digit numeric and single digit alpha
value in feet as whole numbers (XXXXX).
16) Tunnel Curve Grade. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear
text option A: Flat Gradients/ Easy Curves, B: Steep Gradient (>7%), C: Sharp Curves
(Less than 30M), D: Steep Gradients and Sharp Curves
17) Tunnel Grade. Expressed as a two-digit numeric value in percentage (XX%).
18) Tunnel Alignment. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text
option; S: Straight, C: Curve (with radius) activates a box to input the numeric value.
19) Tunnel Lining Surface. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear
text option A: Concrete, C: Brick, D: Stone, E: Crushed Rock, F: Water bound Macadum,
G: Gravel, H: Lightly Metaled, I: Natural or Stabilized Soil, J: Other (activates text box for
50 characters) (option B omitted from the list).
20) Tunnel Ventilation. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text
option, (1: Yes, 0: N).
21) Tunnel Ventilation Type. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the
clear text option; W: Wind Turbine, P: Emergency Access Ports (input interval between
ports – text box appears when this selection is made)
22) Tunnel Drainage. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text
option: Y or (1: Yes, 0: N).
23) Tunnel Drainage Media. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice
recording of the drainage system. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single
digit code (1: Yes, 0: N).
24) Tunnel Demolition. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text
option; Is the tunnel chambered for demolition: (1: Yes, 0: N).
25) Tunnel Completion Date. Expressed as date CCYYMMMDD.

56

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
26) Tunnel Overall Condition. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the
clear text option; A: Excellent, B: Good, C: Fair, D: Poor
27) Tunnel Bypass. If the tunnel can be reasonably bypassed (1: Yes, 0: N).
28) Bypass Grid. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
29) Alternate Crossing Grid. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
30) In Tunnel Restrictions. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear
text option; A: Radius of curves, B: Steep grades, C: Obstacles, D: Roadway width, E:
Combination of restrictions.
31) Portal to Portal Length. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
32) Centerline Distance of Tunnel. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
33) Rise of Tunnel Arch. Expressed as a five-digit numeric and single digit alpha value in
feet as whole numbers (XXXXX).
34) Portal View. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text option;
A: Square with arched ceiling, B: Elliptical, C: Horseshoe, D: Semicircular.
35) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the tunnel
outside of data provided.
36) Attachment. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice recording of
the maintenance condition. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit
code (1: Yes, 0: N).

3.7.3.6 Engineer Reconnaissance – Bridge Report (Site/Structure)
The bridge report is supplemental to the road report or a rail network evaluation.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.
2) Location/Position Information. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
58

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Attached media/object/free is needed for
specific approach/cover and concealment/obstacles/Observations.
3) Start Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
4) End Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
5) Gap Width. Expressed as a five-digit numeric and single digit alpha value in feet as
whole numbers (XXXXX).
6) Clearance. Expressed as a five-digit numeric and single digit alpha value in feet as
whole numbers (XXXXX).
7) Bridge Name. Clear text box entry up to 50 characters if the bridge has a known name.
8) Bridge Direction. Expressed as a two-digit code. First digit is S: Single direction or B:
Bidirectional and second digit equates to actual cardinal direction for single direction: E:
East, W: West, N: North, S: South and 1: East/West or 2: North/South for bidirectional
bridges.
9) Bridge Serial/Number. If the bridge has a corresponding number expressed as a sevendigit alpha-numeric value with special characters (XXXXXX).
10) Bridge/Tunnel Connector. If the bridge it connected to a tunnel (1: Yes, 0: N).
11) Bridge Length. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole numbers
(XXXXX).
12) Bridge Type. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear text
option; 1: Road, 2: Rail, 3: Pedestrian
13) Bridge Bypass. If the bridge can be reasonably bypassed (1: Yes, 0: N).
14) Bypass Grid. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
15) Bridge Tracks. Number of tracks expressed as two-digit numeric value as whole
numbers (XX).
16) Roadway Bridge Lanes. Number of lanes expressed as a two-digit numeric value as
whole numbers (XX).
17) Roadway Bridge Width. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).

59

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
18) Under Bridge Clearance. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
19) Bridge Vertical Clearance. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
20) Bridge Horizontal Clearance. Expressed as a five-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXXXX).
21) Total Number of Bridge Spans. Expressed as a three-digit numeric value as whole
numbers (XXX).
22) Bridge Span Construction. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the
clear text option; A: Truss, B: Girder, C: Beam, D: Slab, E: Arch – Closed Spandrel, F:
Arch – Open Spandrel, G: Suspension, H: Floating, J: Trunnion Swing, K: Single Leaf
Trunnion Bascule, L: Rolling Lift Bascule, M: Double Trunnion Bascule, N: Vertical Life,
P: Other (opens text box).
23) Bridge Span Material. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the clear
text option A: Steel, B: Concrete, C: Reinforced Concrete, D: Prestressed Concrete, F:
Stone, G: Brick, H: Wood, J: Other (activates text box for 50 characters).
24) Attachment. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice recording of
the maintenance condition. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit
code (1: Yes, 0: N).
25) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the bridge
outside of data provided.

3.7.3.7 Engineer Reconnaissance – Ford Report
Usually part of a route report, the ford report presents best possible areas of crossing a water
feature of some kind without a gap crossing solution in place.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.
2) Location/Position Information. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Attached media/object/free is needed for
specific approach/cover and concealment/obstacles/Observations.
3) Start Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.

61

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
4) End Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
5) Minimum Width. Expressed as a five-digit numeric user inputted value in feet (XXXXX).
6) Minimum Depth. Expressed as a two-digit numeric user inputted value in feet (XX).
7) Ford Bottom Type. Expressed as a single-digit alpha value once the user selects the
clear text value M: Mud, C: Clay, S: Sand, G: Gravel, R: Rock, P: Artificial Paving.
8) Route Number. If the ford is connected to an established route expressed as a threedigit numeric entry (XXX).
9) Ford Type. Expressed single-digit numeric value when the user selects the clear text
option P: Pedestrian, V: Vehicular.
10) Stream Velocity. Expressed as a double data input with first single-digit alpha value
when the user selects the clear text option S: Swift, M: Moderate, L: Slow, and second
data input of measured flow rate as whole numbers in meters in a numeric two-digit
value (X|XX).
11) Name of River/Stream/Body of Water. Clear text box entry up to 50 characters if the
body of water has a known name.
12) Low Water Measurements. Multiple data input Width: four-digit numeric expressed in
feet (XXXX), Depth: four-digit numeric expressed in feet (XXXX), Velocity: three-digit
numeric measured speed (XXX), Date of Measurement expressed as local date
CCYYMMMDD.
13) Median Water Measurements. Multiple data input Width: four-digit numeric expressed in
feet (XXXX), Depth: four-digit numeric expressed in feet (XXXX), Velocity: three-digit
numeric measured speed (XXX), Date of Measurement expressed as local date
CCYYMMMDD.
14) High Water Measurements. Multiple data input Width: four-digit numeric expressed in
feet (XXXX), Depth: four-digit numeric expressed in feet (XXXX), Velocity: three-digit
numeric measured speed (XXX), Date of Measurement expressed as local date
CCYYMMMDD.
15) Attachment/Media. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice
recording of the ford area. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit code
(1: Yes, 0: N).
16) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the ford
outside of data provided.

3.7.3.8 Engineer Reconnaissance – Ferry Report
Usually part of a route report, the ferry report presents best possible options to cross large water
features efficiently when organic lift is unsuitable or unavailable.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.
2) Ferry Route Start Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid
Reference System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position
3-4: Alpha (100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location)
depending on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9:
Numeric (Easting) and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be
pre-loaded as a predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for
ease of use.
3) Ferry Route End Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid
Reference System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position
3-4: Alpha (100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location)
depending on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9:
Numeric (Easting) and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be
pre-loaded as a predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for
ease of use.
4) Waterway Velocity. Expressed as a double data input with first single-digit alpha value
when the user selects the clear text option S: Swift, M: Moderate, L: Slow, and second
data input of measured flow rate as whole numbers in meters in a numeric two-digit
value (X|XX).
5) Crossing Distance. Expressed as a three-digit numeric value in miles as whole numbers
(XXX).
6) Ferry Crossing Time. Total time to cross in one direction expressed in 24-hour clock time
as follows: DDHHMM, where D = days (0-99), H = hours (00-23), M = minutes (00-59). If

63

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
the ferry crossing is greater than 24 hours, the DD entry is used however, the default is
zero.
7) Ferry Terminal Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
8) Route Number. If the ferry is connected to an established route expressed as a threedigit numeric entry (XXX).
9) Ferry Type. Expressed single-digit numeric value when the user selects the clear text
option P: Pedestrian, V: Vehicular.
10) Name of River/Stream/Body of Water. Clear text box entry up to 50 characters if the
body of water has a known name.
11) Vessel Condition. Expressed single-digit numeric value when the user selects the clear
text option E: Excellent, F: Fair, P: Poor.
12) Vessel Information. Registration Number, Operating Length, Operating Width, Operating
Tonnage, Vehicle Deadweight Capacity, Railcar Deadweight Capacity
13) Terminal Condition. Expressed single-digit numeric value when the user selects the
clear text option E: Excellent, F: Fair, P: Poor.
14) Terminal Entrance Condition. Expressed single-digit numeric value when the user
selects the clear text option E: Excellent, F: Fair, P: Poor.
15) Terminal Entrance Width. Expressed as a three-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXX).
16) Terminal Entrance Depth. Expressed as a three-digit numeric value in feet as whole
numbers (XXX).
17) Terminal Approach Surface Type. Expressed as a single digit code when the user
selects the clear text option A: Concrete, B: Bituminous, C: Brick, D: Stone, E: Crushed
Rock, F: Water bound Macadum, G: Gravel, H: Lightly Metaled, J: Natural or Stabilized
Soil, K: Other (activates text box for 50 characters)
18) Flooding Risk. If ferry operations are at risk by the condition, expressed single-digit
alpha value when the user selects the clear text option H: Excellent, F: Fair, L: Low.
19) Freezing Risk. If ferry operations are at risk by the condition, expressed single-digit
alpha value when the user selects the clear text option H: Excellent, F: Fair, L: Low.
20) Tidal Risk. If ferry operations are at risk by the condition, expressed single-digit alpha
value when the user selects the clear text option H: Excellent, F: Fair, L: Low.
21) Water Trafficability. Expressed in a fixed 6 position alpha configuration “go” or “slow-go”
or “no-go”.
22) Attachment/Media. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice
recording of the ford area. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit code
(1: Yes, 0: N).

64

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
23) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the ford
outside of data provided.

3.7.3.9 Engineer Reconnaissance – River Report
Usually part of a route report, the river/stream report presents best possible emplacement of
gap crossing options when required or requested by higher-echelon command and control
elements. Additionally, the river report can also serve as a more detailed report when
considering water sources for bulk water purposes or for potential bivouac sites. This report can
also be used in conjunction with the ford report.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.
2) Initial Start Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
3) Route End Point Location. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)

65

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
4) Route Number. If the river is connected to an established route expressed as a threedigit numeric entry (XXX).
5) Name of River/Stream. Clear text box entry up to 50 characters if the body of water has
a known name.
6) General River/Stream Flow Direction. 1: East to West, 2: West to East, 3: North to
South, 4: South to North.
7) Water Trafficability. Expressed in a fixed sing position alpha configuration A: “go”, B:
“slow-go”, or C: “no-go”.
8) Waterway Velocity. Expressed as a double data input with first single-digit alpha value
when the user selects the clear text option S: Swift, M: Moderate, L: Slow, and second
data input of measured flow rate as whole numbers in meters in a numeric two-digit
value (X|XX).
9) Near shore Bank Height. Expressed as a two-digit numeric value in feet (XX).
10) Near shore Bank Slope. Expressed as a two-digit numeric value in degrees (XX).
11) Near shore Bank Stability. Expressed as a single-digit value after the user selects the
clear text option F: Firm, S: Soft, U: Unstable.
12) Nearshore Bank Soil Type. Expressed as a single-digit alpha value once the user
selects the clear text value M: Mud, C: Clay, S: Sand, G: Gravel, R: Rock, P: Artificial
Paving.
13) Far Shore Bank Height. Expressed as a two-digit numeric value in feet (XX).
14) Far Shore Bank Slope. Expressed as a two-digit numeric value in degrees (XX).
15) Far Shore Bank Stability. Expressed as a single-digit alpha value when the user selects
the clear text option F: Firm, S: Soft, U: Unstable.
16) Far Shore Bank Soil Type. Expressed as a single-digit alpha value once the user selects
the clear text value M: Mud, C: Clay, S: Sand, G: Gravel, R: Rock, P: Artificial Paving.
17) Attachment/Media. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice
recording of the ford area. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit code
(1: Yes, 0: N).
18) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the ford
outside of data provided.

3.7.3.10 Engineer Reconnaissance – Landing Zone Report
The landing zone report is an evaluation of a section of usable terrain for the use of aircraft to
land and take off. The landing zone report is not intended to evaluate existing airfields and
facilities for aircraft staging, maintenance, etc.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.
2) Location/Position Information. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Attached media/object/free is needed for
specific approach/cover and concealment/obstacles/Observations.
3) Estimate. Expressed as a single digit code (1: Yes, 0: No)
4) Layout Designation. Expressed as a two-digit alpha value. (Landing Zone: LZ, Landing
Site: LS, Landing Point: LP)
5) Landing Point Capacity. Expressed as a one-digit numeric value (value = number of
aircraft parking spaces) (1) Single airframe
6) Landing Zone Capacity. Expressed as a one-digit numeric value (value = number of
aircraft parking spaces) (1) Single airframe, (2-3) multiple airframes.
7) Landing Site Capacity. Expressed as a one-digit numeric value (value = number of
aircraft parking spaces) (1) Single airframe, (2-4) multiple airframes.
8) Landing Zone Width. Expressed as a three-digit numeric value in feet as whole numbers
(XXX).

67

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
9) Landing Zone Length. Expressed as a four-digit numeric value in feet as whole numbers
(XXX).
10) Aircraft Supportability. Automated calculation based on Landing Zone width and length.
Expressed as a single-digit alpha value indicating rotor diameter. A/B = Size 4 (38’-78’
Aircraft) Aircraft, C/D = Size 2 (44’-59’ Aircraft), E/F Vertical Lift (Requires VTOL).
11) Landing Zone Approach. Expressed single-digit alpha value when the user selects the
clear text option S: South, E: East, N: North, W: West.
12) Landing Zone Departure. Expressed single-digit alpha value when the user selects the
clear text option S: South, E: East, N: North, W: West.
13) Landing Zone Surface Slope. Expressed as a single digit code when the user selects the
clear text option A: <7o up slope landing B: >7o side slope landing.
14) Obstacle. Expressed in single digit code when the user selects the clear text option 1:
remove, 2: reduce, 3: emplace.
15) Attachment/Media. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice
recording of the ford area. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit code
(1: Yes, 0: N).
16) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the ford
outside of data provided.

3.7.3.11 General Engineering – Obstacle Removal
Obstacles refer to any physical characteristics of the terrain that impede the mobility of a force
along a route, road, or pathway. All obstacles are existing or reinforcing. Existing obstacles are
inherent aspects of the terrain and can be natural, man-made, or a combination of both.
1) Date of Evaluation/Reconnaissance. Expressed as local date CCYYMMMDD assuming
midnight to 23:59 as a full day.

68

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
2) Location/Position Information. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Attached media/object/free is needed for
specific approach/cover and concealment/obstacles/Observations.
3) Obstacle. Expressed in single digit code when the user selects the clear text option 1:
Remove, 2: Reduce, 3: Emplace.
4) Minimum/Maximum Length. Expressed as a double data input with first five-digit numeric
minimum value and the second five-digit numeric maximum value if feet
(XXXXX/XXXXX).
5) Minimum/Maximum Width. Expressed as a double data input with first five-digit numeric
minimum value and the second five-digit numeric maximum value in feet
(XXXXX/XXXXX).
6) Minimum/Maximum Depth. Expressed as a double data input with first five-digit numeric
minimum value and the second five-digit numeric maximum value in feet
(XXXXX/XXXXX).
7) Route Number. If the obstacle close to a connected or established route expressed as a
three-digit numeric entry (XXX).
8) Determination of Action: Engineer recommendation of action based on feasibility, risk,
and materials available (used to inform commander’s decision). Expressed in one-digit
numerical value 1: Use bypass, 2: Neutralize Obstacle, 3: Breach, 4: Continue Mission
9) Bypass. If the obstacle can be reasonably bypassed (1: Yes, 0: N).
10) Bypass Grid. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System
(MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100Kmeter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on
accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., White Beach, Pier 3, etc.) for ease of use.
11) Attachment/Media. Expressed as an embedded object of a video, picture, or voice
recording of the ford area. Flag indicator if there is an attachment with a single digit code
(1: Yes, 0: N).
12) Narrative. Free text for additional information up to 100 characters to describe the ford
outside of data provided.

3.8 Health Services Data Requirements
Health services is one of the more data-driven logistics functions requiring accurate and realtime to near real-time information about patients, especially in forward operating locations.
Unfortunately, the health services function is the least understood function of logistics in the
Marine Corps due to a dependence on U.S. Navy (USN) capabilities and lack of education
thereof. This has created a twofold problem in functional understanding:
1) The USMC does not understand its own current service-aligned health service support
(HSS) requirements and has made USMC programs of record largely inaccessible to
naval personnel. Naval personnel are inadequately integrated into the Marine Corps
digital environment. For example, Training and Readiness (T&R) Standards for Hospital
Corpsman are listed in MCTIMS, but commands are not ensuring their sailors meet
those standards, or that their proficiency is properly documented.
2) The USN does not adequately communicate organizational structure, training, and
equipment shortfalls to their USMC commanders.
Therefore, battlefield data collection in the realm of health services is severely lacking, with no
digital tools available to first responders, who primarily rely on analog, paper solutions.
Additionally, the understanding of the flow of care, the actions of Medical C2, and the supporting
data exchange requirements are not integrated into operational impacts and capabilities.
The below graphic depicts the functional layout of health services within the tactical operating
environment and the relationship within the sub-functions. This helps to illustrate the operating
cycle within the health services function and how the sub-functions repeat until resolution.

73

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004

Figure 17: Health Services Cycle

3.8.1 Functional Interdependencies
3.8.1.1 Mobility
The movement and evacuation of casualties to/from/in between medical care areas/facilities are
completely interdependent on the function of mobility and the ability to plan the fastest and most
efficient mode of transportation. While forward units may have access to ground designated
transportation (i.e., ambulances), all other modes of transportation must be planned,
coordinated, and assigned by those working within the capacity planning sub-function.
3.8.1.2 Supply
Medical resources, specifically Class VIII (such as specialized equipment and supplies), are
usually sourced through the Medical Logistics Company of the supporting logistics combat
element (LCE). Resourcing is a critical Medical C2 function to maintain and sustain the
continuum of care from the leading tactical edge throughout the operating environment.
Therefore, the procurement, storage, and distribution of materiel resources within the medical
care network is interdependent on the supply function to establish the required supply chains
and data exchanges. Additionally, Medical C2 needs the visibility of relevant supply information
to make strategic decisions as well as the need for rapid resupply of items to the tactical edge.
3.8.1.3 General Engineering
Beyond Role 1, the Health Services requires facilities, either permanent; semi-permanent; or
temporary to perform medical care safely and efficiently nearest to the point of need. Health
Services is interdependent on the ability of General Engineering for the identification,
rehabilitation, and/or construction of appropriate medical care facilities (other than tents) as well
as the maintenance of such facilities.

3.8.2 Processing Cycle at the Functional Level
The function of health services is multilayered in escalation of medical care under medical C2.
To understand the data exchange requirements for health services requires understanding the
roles of care. The following is the definition and responsibilities of each of the four roles:

74

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
3.8.2.1 Role 1
Role 1 (also referred to as unit-level medical care) includes:
1) Immediate lifesaving measures.
2) Disease and nonbattle injury prevention and care.
3) Combat and operational stress preventive measures.
4) Patient location and acquisition (collection).
Treatment is provided by designated unit Corpsman. Major emphasis is placed on those
measures necessary for the patient to return to duty or to stabilize them and allow for
evacuation to the next role of care. These measures include maintaining the airway, stopping
the bleeding, preventing shock, protecting wounds, immobilizing fractures, and other emergency
measures. Escalation of care within this role starts at the point of injury and onward.
1) Self-Aid. All military personnel are trained in a variety of basic first-aid procedures.
These procedures include aid for chemical casualties with particular emphasis on
lifesaving tasks. This training enables the military personnel to apply first aid to alleviate
potential life-threatening situations.
2) Buddy Aid/Combat Lifesaver Aid.
a. Buddy aid is basic first-aid procedures applied on another individual using the
casualty’s Individual First-Aid Kit (IFAK) or other available medical supplies (issued
and/or improvised).
b. Combat lifesavers are non-medical military personnel selected by their unit
commander for additional training beyond basic first-aid procedures. The primary
duty of this individual does not change. The additional duty of the combat lifesaver is
to provide enhanced first aid for injuries, based on Tactical Combat Casualty Care
(TCCC) protocols and unit issued Combat Life Saver (CLS) medical kits, prior to the
arrival of unit Corpsmen or other medical personnel.
3) Medical Personnel (Corpsman) Aid. Role 1 provides primary healthcare, specialized first
aid, triage, resuscitation, and stabilization. Normally included within the basic Role 1
capabilities are routine sick call and the management of minor sick and injured
personnel who can immediately return to duty. Role 1 also includes casualty collection
and preparation of casualty’s evacuation. Expanded medical treatment is provided by
medical personnel with enhanced medical skills (i.e., Independent Duty Corpsman (IDC),
Independent Duty Medical Technician (IDMT), or physician).
3.8.2.2 Role 2
Role 2 provides advanced trauma management and emergency medical treatment, including
continuation of resuscitation started in Role 1. Role 2 provides a greater capability to resuscitate
trauma patients than is available at Role 1. If necessary, additional emergency measures are
initiated, but they do not go beyond the measures dictated by immediate necessities. Role 2
care has the capability to provide packed blood products, limited X-ray, laboratory, dental
support, combat and operational stress control, preventative medicine (PVTMED), and
resuscitative surgical support. Role 2 has a limited hold capability necessitating the onward
evacuation of casualties.

75

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
3.8.2.3 Role 3
In Role 3, the patient is treated in medical treatment facility (MTF) staffed and equipped to
provide care to all categories of patients, to include resuscitation, initial wound surgery, specialty
surgery (general, orthopedic, urogenital, thoracic, ENT, neurosurgical) and post-operative
treatment. This may include definitive surgery for local nationals depending on the current rules
of engagement. This role of care expands the support provided at Role 2. Patients who are
unable to tolerate and survive movement over long distances receive surgical care in a hospital
as close to the supported unit as the tactical situation allows. This role includes provisions for:
1) Evacuating patients from supported units.
2) Providing care for all categories of patients in a MTF with the proper staff and
equipment.
3) Providing area medical support to units without organic medical assets.
3.8.2.4 Role 4
Role 4 medical care is found in U.S. hospitals and robust overseas facilities. These hospitals
represent the most comprehensive medical care available to restore the individual to operational
duty, or medically retire the individual for continuing, long term care.
3.8.2.5 Role Data Similarities
Each of the roles are executing similar functions in collection, treatment, holding, and then
finally evacuation. The initial evacuation from Role 1 to Role 2 would be a casualty evacuation
(CASEVAC), however, once in the medical care system each subsequent evacuation is
classified as a medical evacuation (MEDEVAC). If the patient is ambulatory, this is simply a
PAX request. Therefore, no matter the role level, each data set is building upon the last role’s
data set in identifying the casualty, the injury, resulting treatment at each role, and subsequent
movement. While casualty management is the function of health services, casualty tracking is
the function of command services. This is currently a data layer gap between the Health
Services function and Services function of logistics.
3.8.2.6 Medical Data Limitations
DoD has mandated use of paper forms for patient/casualty data capture, to include DD Form
1380 and DA Form 7656, and TCCC Cards. The DoD’s intent is as follows:
1) All data from these cards are expected to be manually-transcribed into the
servicemember’s electronic health record (EHR). While well intentioned, the expectation
of analog data collected in the field to be then input into a digital record is unrealistic and
prone to human error.
2) Services are to review and update current service-specific doctrine and training plans to
incorporate use of the physical TCCC cards in pre-hospital and organizational first aid
provided by both medical and non-medical first responders. However, non-medical first
responders need continuous training to orient on and understand the complexities of
medical abbreviations and definitions to accurately collect the relevant data.
3) Services are to coordinate with the Director, Defense Health Agency (DHA), to facilitate
the development and deployment of an electronic version of the TCCC card. Again,
these efforts have centered around and are limited to electromechanical variations of the
paper card, appearing as fillable portable document formats (PDF). PDFs are not truly
digital records. Additionally, it is highly unlikely that medical responders will have mobile
devices with the PDF version of the TCCC card while forward deployed, and how such

76

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
data would be transmitted from the device to the next MTF and then transcribed into the
casualty’s EHR.
4) Since the TCCC card is a physical item, services are to ensure a physical TCCC card is
stocked in organizational medical equipment sets, kits, and outfits to include CLS bags,
IFAKs/JFAKs, and Unit First Aid Kits located on all operational platforms. Additionally,
DHA requires the stocking of TCCC cards with expediency to support the appropriate
documentation of care in the pre-hospital environment during all contingencies. The
requirement for physical data capture cards comes with real cost to produce, space to
store, and forecasting for re-stocking. This creates additional and unnecessary burden
on the supply chain.

3.8.3 Data Exchange Requirements at Role 1 (pre-MTF)
Every role level exhibits the same process of collection, treatment, hold, and evacuation. Within
the scope of the analysis, the actions at Role 1 are the building blocks for the data continuum
throughout the patient’s continuum of care, originating at the most forward tactical edge.
Through analysis, the actions performed at Role 1 of collection, treatment, hold, and evacuation
are all occurring, however, each stage in the process may be compressed or reduced due to
situational urgency. Therefore, the data exchange requirement at each stage in the process are
independent actions building on itself as a digital record. While recognizing each stage may be
compressed to some point, the data flow appears as one seamless fluid action.
The collected data must be easily and seamlessly passed between care providers via local
machine to local machine and/or to the next level of care. The next level of care should receive
the casualty data prior to arrival of the patient, vice the data following in trace. The data
originating in digital record at the point of injury serves as the basis of decision in continuing
health care conclusions and enables effective/efficient Medical C2.
The initial buildout of available medications to first responders must be an automated process,
completed prior to the execution of an exercise, operation, deployment. All data comprising a
health services request must automatically update the servicemembers’ electronic health record
and be accessible and available at every level of care. If care is provided to an individual that is
not within the service care network, or on an unregistered casualty (EPW, NON-US, US-CIV,
etc.), a skeleton record is built based on the input data for later merging, updating, and/or
archiving.
3.8.3.1 Collection
Casualties are assembled at a predetermined location, or at a location of opportunity to protect
from further injury. Data recorded at the point of collection are:
1) Segment Number. System assigned as the request is created under the header. A single
digit indicator: up to nine independent request types can be added under the header.
The segment number does not restrict the number of patients/casualties being reported
or CASEVAC requested.
2) Request Type. Expressed as a two-digit background code when the user selects
“Casualty Report”. In this case CR is the code for an injury/casualty/illness report.
3) Request Priority. Expressed as two-digit code based on the urgency aligned to the
element/unit’s F/AD. Auto populated based on Triage Precedence: A and/or B = Critical,
C = Urgent, D and/or E = Routine
4) ZAP/EDI-PI. Expressed as either 8 to 9-digit ZAP or 10-digit EDI-PI. ZAP data element is
a preformatted and system assigned abbreviation for USMC personnel. EDI-PI is DoD

77

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
assigned for all DoD personnel (active, reserve, government service [GS], and
contractor). User should not necessarily need to type in these identifiers but select from
a preloaded list on the local machine or scan a government (U.S. Federal, Local, and/or
foreign Passport/ID) issued identification card if the individual is not in the list.
5) Last Name. Auto populated from the local machine list if the ZAP/EDI-PI is resident. If
not, input text box up to 15 characters for non-military U.S. or other. This information is
passed only if the input text box is activated.
6) First Name. Auto populated from the local machine list if the ZAP/EDI-PI is resident. If
not, input text box up to 15 characters for non-military U.S. or other. This information is
passed only if the input text box is activated.
7) Service. Casualty’s branch of service: Auto populated from the local machine list if the
ZAP/EDI-PI is resident. If not, input text box with the following codes: USA, USSF,
USAF, USCG, USN, USMC. For U.S. civilians (GS, contractor, etc.): US CIV. For nonU.S. Coalition and NATO personnel (military and civilian): NON-US. Enemy Prisoner of
War: EPW. This information is passed only if the input text box is activated.
8) Element/Unit Identification/Call Sign. Injured/casualty’s element/unit/call sign (not the
reporting unit/element) if U.S military is auto populated from the local machine list if the
ZAP/EDI-PI is resident. Expressed as a four-digit alpha-numeric reference key which
aligns to the clear text naming convention. The clear text naming convention does not
need to be passed, only the unique index key which was randomly assigned by system.
The origination of callsigns/brevity codes for units/elements is with the operations
function. This stresses the importance of operation planning and execution occurring in a
digital environment. If not, input text box up to 15 characters. This information is passed
only if the input text box is activated.
9) Allergies/Alerts. Ideally auto populated from source personnel medical records to the
local machine prior to deployment. If transcribing from red medical tag, this becomes a
text box for manual input up to 30 characters. No need to identify as “allergy” as the field
is labeled and identified as the type of information when synchronized to the enterprise
system. Example: if a red tag is found on the casualty indicating an allergy to penicillin,
simply input “penicillin”. This information is passed only if the input text box is activated.
Auto populates with “NKDA” (no known drug allergies).
10) Date of Injury. Local: Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD. Defaults to the current date of
the entry but can be overridden to a previous day.
11) Time of Injury. Local: System time expressed in 24-hour clock time as follows: HHMM, or
HHMMSS, or HHMMSSD, or HHMMSSDD, where H = hours (00-23), M = minutes (0059), S = integer seconds (00-59) and DD = decimal seconds; decimal seconds are
expressed as follows: D = tenths (0-9) and DD = hundredths (00-99). SS and DD are
inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to the current time of
the entry but can be overridden to a previous time.
12) Location Injury Occurred. Geospatial reference expressed in Military Grid Reference
System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha (Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha
(100K-meter Square Identifier), Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending
on accuracy level within 1-, 10-, and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting)
and position 10-14: Numeric (Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a
predetermined clear text descriptor (i.e., Hill 588, etc.) for ease of use, estimated
location is acceptable as well as “pin drop” current location.

Table 33: Health Services - Collection Data

3.8.3.2 Treatment
Treatment includes the triage and application of care from self-aid through Role 4 capabilities.
Triage is the process of casualty sorting and is basic to the successful operation of a patient
movement system. Rapid evaluations must be made to identify which patients need immediate
resuscitation and which patients can tolerate delay in treatment. After triage, treatment is
applied to sustain the casualty until the next level of care. The following data elements are two
separate actions within the same function and will be presented as “triage” and then “treatment.”
The intent is to continue the record of data initiated at the point of collection. As the data is
collected it can be easily categorized, arranged, and sorted as the user interface requires. For
instance, the input data fields can be arranged to meet the MARCH-PAWS algorithm of care.
13) Primary Mechanism of Injury: Expressed as a main category and then a secondary
category:
a. Main Category 1. Injury by explosive. Indicates a rapid expansion of heated gases,
solids, and/or liquids. Explosive effects on the body carry the possibility of shrapnel,
concussive injuries, hemorrhaging, burns, and/or Chemical, Biological or
Radiological vectors. Clear text selection is a two-digit code: E1: artillery/Indirect fire,
grenade, E2: IED (improvised explosive device), E3: landmine, E4: RPG (rocket
propelled grenade), and E5: other type of explosion.
b. Main Category 2. Injury by a physical force. Effects of gravitational, velocity, and/or
centrifugal forces. Effects of the body are lacerations, hemorrhaging, compression
injuries, bruising, and/or fractures/breakage. Clear text selection is a two-digit code:
P1: blunt force trauma, P2: fall, P3: velocity impact (e.g., vehicular crash/accident),
P4: GSW (gunshot wound), and P5: knife/bayonet/sharp object.
c. Main Category 3. Injury by illness/disease. Effects of abnormalities in the function
and/or structure of body organs and systems. Effects on the body are lack of bodily
control, extreme discomfort, choking, blistering, disorientation, and/or mental
soundness. Clear text selection is a two-digit code: D1: pathogen (viral, bacterial,
fungi, protozoa), D2: allergic reaction, D3: chemical/biological hazard exposure D4:
pathological.
14) CBRN Related/Exposure. Expressed as a single code entry if casualty’s injury has been
caused by CBRN vectors and/or the casualty has been or is suspected to have been

79

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
exposed to a CBRN environment. C: Chemical, B: Biological, R: Radiological, N:
Nuclear, X: None. System defaults to X: None
15) Major Signs/Symptoms. Expressed as a clear text selection with a single digit code: B:
bleeding, R: restricted breathing, X: burned, C: incapacitation. If “burn” is selected this
will provide an overall calculated surface area estimate body percentage based on
“Injury Location(s).”
16) Injury Location(s). User selects clear text entry which is converted into a three-digit data
code for transmission. Only one area can be selected (one front head, one back head,
one front chest, one back chest, etc.). Additionally, the selected location provides a burn
estimate for calculation in parenthesis [XXX (XX)]: FH0 (4.5): Front Head (4.5), FH1:
Front Head Ears, Nose, Throat, FH2 (4.5): Front Head Eyes, FH3 (4.5): Front Head
Dental, BH0 (4.5): Back of the Head, FN0 (4.5): Front Neck, BN0 (4.5): Back Neck, C00
(18): Chest, RC0 (09): Right Chest, LC0 (09): Left Chest (09), CC0 (09): Center Chest,
B00 (18): Back, UB0 (09): Upper Back, LB0 (09): Lower Back, LA0 (4.5): Left Arm, RA0
(4.5): Right Arm, LL0 (09): Left Leg, RL0 (09): Right Leg, G00 (01): Groin, P00 (01):
Posterior, A00 (09): Abdominal
17) Triage/Treatment Vitals Check Date – Local. Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD.
Defaults to the current date of the entry. This serves as a sub-heading for the six vitals
checked at the time of triage/treatment.
18) Triage/Treatment Vitals Check Time – Local. System time expressed in 24-hour clock
time as follows: HHMM, or HHMMSS, or HHMMSSD, or HHMMSSDD, where H = hours
(00-23), M = minutes (00-59), S = integer seconds (00-59) and DD = decimal seconds;
decimal seconds are expressed as follows: D = tenths (0-9) and DD = hundredths (0099). SS and DD are inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to
the current time of the entry.
19) Body Temperature. Expressed as a three-digit whole number in Fahrenheit. System
convertible to Celsius.
20) Pulse Rate/Location. Comprised of two data points. Pulse Rate: Expressed as a threedigit whole number. Pulse Location: Expressed as a single alpha code corresponding to
the clear text selection W: Wrist (radial artery), N: Neck (carotid artery). XXX|X
21) Blood Pressure. Expressed as two sets of three-digit numbers (systolic and diastolic)
with a pipe separator in between: XXX|XXX.
22) Respiratory Rate. Count of chest rises in a one minute while the casualty is at rest.
Expressed as a two-digit numeric entry: XX.
23) Pulse Oximetry % O2 Saturation. Expressed as two-digit whole numbers in a percentage
usually from 90-99%: XX.
24) Responsiveness. Expressed with a clear text selection with a background single alpha
code A: alert, V: responds to voice, P: responds to pain, U: unresponsive.
25) Pain Scale. If the casualty is alert or voice responsive a pain scale can be employed.
The pain scale is a double numeric digit expressed as follows: 0: No pain, 1: Pain is very
mild, barely noticeable. Most of the time the casualty doesn't think about it. 2: Minor pain.
It's annoying. The casualty has a sharp pain now and then. 3: Noticeable pain.
Distracting but the casualty gets used to it. 4: Moderate pain. If the casualty is involved
in an activity, they can ignore the pain for a while, but it is still distracting. 5: Moderately
strong pain. The casualty can't ignore it for more than a few minutes. But, with effort, the

80

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
casualty can still work or do some moderate activities. 6: Moderately stronger pain. The
casualty avoids some normal daily activities and has trouble concentrating. 7: Strong
pain. Casualty cannot perform normal activities. 8: Very strong pain. The casualty cannot
perform any work or activities at all. 9: Pain that is very hard to tolerate. The casualty
cannot or has difficulty carrying on a conversation.10: Worst pain possible.
26) Triage Precedence. Expressed with a clear text selection with a single alpha code. A:
Urgent (surgical) - requires surgery while enroute to the MTF. B: Urgent (non-surgical) patient can be stabilized until arrival to MTF. C: Priority - injuries that are not immediately
life-threatening but could become life-threatening if medical care is not provided. D:
Routine - non-life-threatening medical care beyond unit’s ability, or deceased patient. E:
Convenience - non-life-threatening care provided to personnel in austere conditions but
requires professional medical evaluation. Note: If a tourniquet has been selected as a
treatment type, the triage precedence defaults to B – Urgent (Non-Surgical), as a lower
precedence cannot be applied. The precedence can be overridden to increase to A –
Urgent (Surgical) by user intervention.

27) Extremity Bleeding Treatment (Tourniquets). Data set is a four-part series for placement,
type, date, and time. All four parts must be recorded for a complete entry. The
placement is the base or header data element with the type, date, and time being the
subordinate and required data elements.
a. Placement. Clear text selection correlating to a four-digit alpha data code for
transmission. No tourniquets: TQXX, Right Arm: TQRA, Left Arm: TQLA, Right Leg:
TQRL, and Left Leg: TQLL
b. Type. Type of tourniquet applied is a single digit alpha code in response to the user’s
clear text input. The data element is the fifth data element in the string. E: extremity,
J: junctional, and T: truncal
c. Date – Local. Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD. Defaults to the current date of the
entry but can be overridden to a previous day.
d. Time – Local. System time expressed in 24-hour clock time as follows: HHMM, or
HHMMSS, or HHMMSSD, or HHMMSSDD, where H = hours (00-23), M = minutes

(00-59), S = integer seconds (00-59) and DD = decimal seconds; decimal seconds
are expressed as follows: D = tenths (0-9) and DD = hundredths (00-99). SS and DD
are inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to the current
time of the entry but can be overridden to an earlier time.
28) Wounds Treatment: (Bandaging/Dressing). User selected clear text input provides
background the corresponding code for date exchange Hemostatic Dressing: T1,
Pressure Bandage: T2, Sling: T3, Splint: T3, Eye Shield (Left): T4, Eye Shield Right: T5,
Eye Shield Both: T6, Hypothermia Prevention: T7
29) Airway Treatment. Information concerning the airway and treatments are expressed as
two-digit alpha-numeric codes for data exchange when the user selects the clear text
input. Airway Intact: A0, NPA (nasopharyngeal airway): A1, CRIC (cricothyroidotomy):
A2, ET-Tube (endotracheal tube): A3, SGA (supraglottic airway): A4
30) Breathing Treatment. Information concerning the breathing treatments are expressed as
two-digit alpha-numeric codes for data exchange when the user selects the clear text
input. None: B0, O2: B1, Needle-D: B3, Chest Tube: B4, Chest Seal: B5
31) Fluid Circulation Resuscitation Interventions/Treatments. Expressed as a five-part data
series.
a. Fluid Name. Saline: S, Ringer’s Lactate: R, Hextend: H, Other (input clear text name
up to 20 characters)
b. Volume/Dose. Expressed as a four-digit numeric whole number for milliliters or cubic
centimeters.
c. Route. IV: Intravenous, IO: Interosseous
d. Date – Local. Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD. Defaults to the current date of the
entry but can be overridden to a previous day.
e. Time – Local. System time expressed in 24-hour clock time as follows: HHMM, or
HHMMSS, or HHMMSSD, or HHMMSSDD, where H = hours (00-23), M = minutes
(00-59), S = integer seconds (00-59) and DD = decimal seconds; decimal seconds
are expressed as follows: D = tenths (0-9) and DD = hundredths (00-99). SS and DD
are inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to the current
time of the entry but can be overridden to an earlier time.
32) Blood Circulation Resuscitation Interventions/Treatments. Expressed as a five-part data
series.
a. Blood Product Name. whole blood: WBD, red blood cells: RBC, fresh frozen plasma:
FFP, lyophilized (freeze-dried) plasma: FDP.
b. Volume/Dose. Expressed as a four-digit numeric whole number for milliliters or cubic
centimeters.
c. Route. IV: Intravenous, IO: Interosseous
d. Date – Local. Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD. Defaults to the current date of the
entry but can be overridden to a previous day.
e. Time – Local. System time expressed in 24-hour clock time as follows: HHMM, or
HHMMSS, or HHMMSSD, or HHMMSSDD, where H = hours (00-23), M = minutes
(00-59), S = integer seconds (00-59) and DD = decimal seconds; decimal seconds
are expressed as follows: D = tenths (0-9) and DD = hundredths (00-99). SS and DD

are inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to the current

Expressed as a five-part data series.
a. Medication Name. Ketamine: K, Fentanyl: F, Morphine: M, Other (input clear text

b. Volume/Dose. Expressed as a two-digit numeric whole number for milliliters or cubic

rectal
d. Date – Local. Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD. Defaults to the current date of the

are inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to the current

a. Medication Name. M: moxifloxacin, E: ertapenem, P: penicillin, A: azithromycin,

c. Route. R1: intrathecal (into the spine), R2: subcutaneous (under the skin), R3:
intravenous (into a vein), R4: intramuscular (into a muscle), R5: oral, R6: inhale, R7:
rectal
d. Date – Local. Date expressed as CCYYMMMDD. Defaults to the current date of the

HHMMSS, or HHMMSSD, or HHMMSSDD, where H = hours (00-23), M = minutes
(00-59), S = integer seconds (00-59) and DD = decimal seconds; decimal seconds
are expressed as follows: D = tenths (0-9) and DD = hundredths (00-99). SS and DD
are inconsequential for this data input and default to “00:00”. Defaults to the current
time of the entry but can be overridden to an earlier time.
35) Other Medication Treatments. Due to the myriad of available medications, it is best if the

Table 35: Health Services - Treatment Data (Intervention Segment)

3.8.3.3 Hold
The holding of casualties for monitoring post-treatment or post-operation for onward care and/or
movement. Holding of a casualty requires monitoring of vitals and administering continuing
treatment methods as required. Additional data requirements are appended to the original
record in terms of vitals and/or administering additional medications/treatments. All
corresponding data elements can have additional date/time entries. No data is overwritten or
deleted but is appended with additional date/time driven data entries.

84

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
3.8.3.4 Evacuate (CASEVAC)
The movement of casualties to and/or between medical treatment facilities. Users select
casualties from an auto generated list produced by the collection process to evacuate on the
local machine. Once all casualties are selected (casualties can be selected from the list by filter
i.e., by precedence, all, etc.) which will initiate the request via data form. The evacuation or
CASEVAC is essential a specialized PAX movement request. When the evacuate request is
initiated, key data elements recorded during the collection, treatment, and hold processes are
brought forward into the request with minimal user intervention. The evacuate request data form
prioritizes data 1) evacuation request (aka legacy 9-Line), 2) priority medical information (aka
legacy Z-MIST), and 3) medical record/casualty report (aka legacy TCCC data collection card).
38) Request Priority. Auto populates based on the highest casualty triage precedence in the
data set. A: Urgent (surgical) - i.e. requires surgeon to perform surgery while enroute to
the MTF, B: Urgent (non-surgical) - i.e. patient can be stabilized until arrival to MTF, C:
Priority - i.e. injuries that are not immediately life threatening but could become life
threatening if medical care is not provided, D: Routine - i.e. non-life threatening medical
care beyond unit’s ability, E: Convenience - i.e. non life-threatening care provided to
personnel in an austere condition but requires professional medical evaluation.
39) Location of Pickup. If predetermined, this can be loaded as a default setting. Geospatial
reference expressed in Military Grid Reference System (MGRS). Position 1-2: Alpha
(Grid Zone Designator, GZD), Position 3-4: Alpha (100K-meter Square Identifier),
Position 5-14: Numeric (Numerical Location) depending on accuracy level within 1-, 10-,
and 100-meter intervals: position 5-9: Numeric (Easting) and position 10-14: Numeric
(Northing). Remarks: Physical can be pre-loaded as a predetermined clear text
descriptor (i.e., Hill 588, etc.) for ease of use or use “pin drop” location.
40) Location Marking. User determines if location needs or will be marked. A: Panels, B:
Pyrotechnic (i.e., flare, red star cluster), C: Smoke (provide smoke color), D: IR flash or
signal beacon, E: None. (Optional, defaults to E: None)
41) Location Contamination. A: Nuclear/Radiological, B: Biological, C: Chemical, D: None
(Optional, defaults to: D: None)
42) Contact Settings. Frequency and call-sign at pickup site. If predetermined, this can be
loaded as a default setting. Defaults to user/element call sign and frequency. Four-digit
callsign and 4-digit frequency setting XXXX|XX.XX
43) Count of Casualties – Precedence. Auto populated, calculated, and sorted by number of
patients by precedence when casualties are selected. Two data elements: single digit
priority and two-digit numeric number. X|XX
44) Count of Casualty – Types. Auto populated, calculated, and sorted by number of
patients by type when casualties are selected. Two data elements: single digit type (A:
ambulatory/L: Litter and two-digit numeric count. X|XX)
45) Requested Equipment. User indicates by clear text if special equipment is required, A:
none, B: hoist, C: extraction equipment, D: ventilation (Optional, defaults to A: None)
46) Security. User determines if location maybe compromised by enemy action. N: No
enemy troops in area, P: Possible enemy troops in area (approach with caution), E:
Enemy troops in area (approach with caution), X: Enemy troops in area (armed escort
required) (Optional, defaults to N: None)

85

Logistics Data Exchange Requirements at the Tactical Edge
FA8075-18-D-0004
47) ZAP/EDI-PI of Casualties/Treatments. Entire data set is auto populated when the
casualties are selected for evacuation. The ZAP/EDI-PI serves a header for the
treatment information. Expressed as either 8 to 9-digit ZAP or 10-digit EDI-PI.
a. Mechanism of injuries auto populated with two-digit code when the casualties are
selected for evacuation.
b. Major injury auto populated with single digit code when the casualties are selected
for evacuation.
c. Signs last recorded readings data set auto populated when the casualties are
selected for evacuation. Body Temperature: three-digit reading, Pulse Rate/Location:
four-digit reading, Blood Pressure: six-digit reading, Respiratory Rate: two-digit
reading.
d. Treatment given (morphine, tourniquet etc.) last recorded readings auto populated
when the casualties are selected for evacuation. Extremity Bleeding Treatment (TQ):
22-digit response X 1-4 occurrences (maximum of four, if applied), Wounds
Treatment: 2 X 1-7 occurrences, Airway Treatment: two-digit code, Breathing
Treatment: two-digit code, Fluid Circulation Treatments: 24 to 34 digit code (last
application only), Blood Circulation Treatments: 24 to 34 digit code (last application
only), Analgesic Medication Treatments: 24 to 34 digit code (last dose only),
Antibiotic Medication Treatments: 24 to 34 digit code (last dose only), Other
Medication Treatments: 24 to 34 digit code (last dose only)
e. Casualty CBRN auto populated single digit code when the casualties are selected for
evacuation.
